        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442413344" href="/book/show/12162432-where-things-come-back">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828294377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9321515415700497728">Let me start off by saying that I think I really wanted to like this book a whole lot more than I did. Don't get me wrong, I did really enjoy this. However, from what I heard about it and expected going into it, I think I wanted this to be a solid 5/5 wonderful, new favorite, etc. And while it was a unique, beautiful, thought-provoking story, I felt like it was just shy of that 100%. <br/><br/>So really I give this more of a 4.5/5. C'mon Goodreads, where is that half star?<br/><br/>This story stands alone from othe</span>
  <span id="freeText9321515415700497728" style="display:none">Let me start off by saying that I think I really wanted to like this book a whole lot more than I did. Don't get me wrong, I did really enjoy this. However, from what I heard about it and expected going into it, I think I wanted this to be a solid 5/5 wonderful, new favorite, etc. And while it was a unique, beautiful, thought-provoking story, I felt like it was just shy of that 100%. <br /><br />So really I give this more of a 4.5/5. C'mon Goodreads, where is that half star?<br /><br />This story stands alone from others. The weaving of two very different and possibly controversial hot topics was intriguing. On one hand we have a disappearance of a child and on the other we have a missionary who falls away from the faith and makes some drastic life decisions. How Whaley pulls these two stories together and intertwines characters was something I didn't see coming although I knew it had to happen about halfway through the book. <br /><br />I enjoyed the writing style. It was sophisticated and elevated yet still understandable and attainable. The main character Cullen had a lot of opinions and philosophical musings which I enjoyed. This book goes beyond just presenting an issue in fictional light and stresses the real life application for the reader to take away from reading it, which I thought was excellent.<br /><br />I want to reread this book already, because I am sure there is more to learn and to not be missed. And also because it is so short I almost wish there had been more to it.<br /><br />4.5/5</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JgRjtDMl/+BzbGZ+EB0/zDXJ1Z72Jut7UlBxjk4BgbccIgpmiHs2iNRH0h/n6DUT45YyVjirZRwJLjc/g0JzLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nxUotssrCse9tf0XLmDBUYNvz54FjPKu1ZbrX7YwxaWlM0FkcHXDrxqeSXbZlcuOVTAoVssBfMmO6K3ue3M3Pw==')})
  }

He and his wife have a baby boy.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4113638.John_Corey_Whaley">About John Corey Whaley</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4113638.John_Corey_Whaley"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1303709143p3/4113638.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13409993875630667972">JOHN ‘COREY’ WHALEY grew up in the small town of Springhill, Louisiana, where he learned to be sarcastic and to tell stories. He has a B.A. in English from Louisiana Tech University, as well as an M.A in Secondary English Education. He started writing stories about aliens and underwater civilizations when he was around ten or eleven, but now writes realistic YA fiction (which sometimes includes zo</span>
  <span id="freeText13409993875630667972" style="display:none">JOHN ‘COREY’ WHALEY grew up in the small town of Springhill, Louisiana, where he learned to be sarcastic and to tell stories. He has a B.A. in English from Louisiana Tech University, as well as an M.A in Secondary English Education. He started writing stories about aliens and underwater civilizations when he was around ten or eleven, but now writes realistic YA fiction (which sometimes includes zombies…). He taught public school for five years and spent much of that time daydreaming about being a full-time writer…and dodging his students’ crafty projectiles. He is terrible at most sports, but is an occasional kayaker and bongo player. He is obsessed with movies, music, and traveling to new places. He is an incredibly picky eater and has never been punched in the face, though he has come quite close. One time, when he was a kid, he had a curse put on him by a strange woman in the arcade section of a Wal-Mart. His favorite word is defenestration. His favorite color is green. His favorite smell is books. He currently splits his time between Louisiana and Los Angeles. <br /><br />Where Things Come Back is his first novel.<br /><br />NOGGIN, his second novel, is out on April 8, 2014. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13409993875630667972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/13432259-where-things-come-back">Quotes from Where Things Come...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Life, he says, doesn’t have to be so bad all the time. We don’t have to be anxious about everything. We can just be. We can get up, anticipate that the day will probably have a few good moments and a few bad ones, and then just deal with it. Take it all in and deal as best we can.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/512348-life-he-says-doesn-t-have-to-be-so-bad-all">232 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Your mind has a way of not letting you forget things you wish you could. Especially with people. Like, you'll always try your best to forget things that people say to you or about you, but you always remember. And you'll try to forget things you've seen that no one should see, but you just can't do it. And when you try to forget someone's face, you can't get it out of your head.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/554912-your-mind-has-a-way-of-not-letting-you-forget">142 likes</a>
            </nobr>
